CERTIFIED RECORDS FROM ANY AND ALL LOCATIONS AND/OR DEPARTMENTS
Dear Records Clerk,
Please be advised that this office has been retained to represent the above referenced Client regarding injuries sustained in a
motor vehicle, premise liability, and/or workers compensation incident. We request that you respond, with acknowledgment of
this letterofrepresentation, within three (3) business days and direct all future correspondence to our office in this matter.
In accordance with Kentucky Revised Statute 422.317, please provide to us, in a sworn statement, any and all medical records
along with the associated billing in your possession up to and including but not limited to the following within thirty (30) days:
1. Any and all office notes, medical history, physicals, consultation notes, discharge summaries, orders and
progress notes.
2. Any and all radiology, pathology, toxicology, oncology or any other laboratory records and results.
3. Any and all nurse's notes, physician notes, emergency records, operative reports/summaries, in-patient notes.
4. Any and all films of x-rays, MRIs, CTs, or PET scans and their associated orders and reports.
5. Any and all pharmacy orders, prescriptions and dispensing logs.
6. Any and all health insurance information or policies of medical coverage.
7. Any and all billing and payment records for each date ofservice.
We have attached a signed HIPPA compliant authorization valid for three (3) years as this is an ongoing request. Please forward
any updated records to our office every thirty (30) days without further requests.
Thank you for your prompt attention to this matter and please do not hesitate to contact me directly at [PHONE-176] or via
email at Sarena@WhaleyLawFirm.com.
Sincerely,
Sarena m. Tuttle

HIPAA COMPLIANT MEDICAL AUTHORIZATION
(Authorization to Release Protected Health Care Information)
To: The Medical Center at Bowling Green
250 Park Street
Bowling Green, KY 42101
Dear Medical Records Clerk:
I have retained The Whaley Law Firm, PSC to represent me in matters related to an injury sustained due to a third parties' negligence. Please
forward a copy ofany &all records not previously provided to The Whaley Law Firm upon request.
Pursuant to the Health Insurance Portability & Accountability Act (HIPAA) Privacy Regulations, 45 CFR 164.508, the provider listed above is
hereby authorized to release to The Whaley Law Firm, PSC or anyoftheir representatives, all medical records, including but not limited to: Office
Notes, History, Physical, Consultation Notes, Discharge Summaries, Orders, Progress Notes, Laboratory Results, Nurses' Notes, Emergency Room
Records, Operative Reports, In-Patient Records and films ofX-Rays, MRIs, CT Scans, or PET Scans, Pharmacy and Drug Records, Medical Bills
and Health Insurance Information, Medicaid/Medicare Records, concerning ANY medical treatment that I have received from you and/or at your
facility, as well as ALL such records which you keep in the regular course of business that are found in my medical record file.
I hereby authorize the release of ANY & ALL records regarding mental health, psychiatric (other than psychotherapy notes, which must be
requested under separate authorization), Chemical Dependency or HIV.
A photostatic copy hereof shall be as valid as the original.
I hereby authorize a FREE COPY of my medical records pursuant to KRS 422.317 be sent to the extent I have not already requested my one free
copy.
The purpose ofthis authorization and request is to permit my attorney to obtain ALL medical information pertaining to my physical and mental
condition(s). This authorization expires in three (3) years from the date ofthe signature. The aforementioned expiration date has not passed, as
this matter is on-going. I hereby authorize The Whaley Law Firm, PSC. to speak to my healthcare providers privately or to take the testimony at
deposition and/or trial as may be requested.
I have the right to revoke this authorization in writing by providing a signed, written notice ofrevocation to the healthcare provider listed above
and to The Whaley Law Firm, PSC. I understand that there are exceptions to the right torevoke. Among the exceptions to the right to revoke are
that an individual may not revoke an authorization to the extent that the covered entity has taken action in reliance thereon. Medical Providers
may not condition treatment or payment on whether the above-listed patient executes this authorization. The information disclosed pursuant to
this authorization may be subject to re-disclosure and no longer protected by the privacy regulations promulgated pursuant to the Health Insurance
Portability and Accountability Act (HIPAA)
DocuSigned by:
Cars Hall [DOB-1]
Chiff SERVICE 72 Date ofBirth
Cora Hall [SSN-1] Date: [DOB-15]

6-Feb-2025 15:54 [PHONE-170] [PHONE-169] p.3
369.107 Legal recognition of electronic records, electronic signatures, and
electronic contracts.
(1) A record or signature may not be denied legal effect or enforceability solely because
itis in electronic form.
(2) A contract may not be denied legal effect or enforceability solely because an
electronic record was used in its formation.
(3) Ifa law requires a record to be in writing, an electronic record satisfies the law.
(4) Ifa law requires a signature, an electronic signature satisfies the law.
Effective: August 1, 2000
History: Created 2000 Ky. Acts ch. 301, sec. 7, effective August 1, 2000.

The Medical Center at Bowling Green 
General Conditions of Admission, Consent, Assignment of Benefits & Financial Agreement 
Consent to Diagnostic Tests, Procedures and Medical Treatment: 
I do voluntarily consent to hospital care involving diagnostic tests, 
procedures and medical treatment as ordered by my treating physician(s), 
practitioner(s) and his or her designees. This consent includes testing for 
communicable diseases, including but not limited to Human 
Immunodeficiency Virus (HIV), hepatitis or any other blood-bome 
infectious disease if ordered for a diagnostic purpose or due to 
occupational exposure of a health care worker. I acknowledge no 
guarantee has been made to me as to the results of examination and 
treatment in the hospital. 
Independent Contractor Acknowledgement: 
I understand and acknowledge the physicians and other practitioners 
involved in my care, including but not limited to my attending 
physician, consulting physicians, emergency department physicians, 
physician assistants, nurse practitioners, radiologists, 
anesthesiologists, nurse anesthetists and pathologists are not agents 
or employees of The Medical Center. I further understand I will be 
billed separately for services by these providers. These providers have 
independent relationships with insurance companies, and the hospital 
makes no guarantee as to any preferred provider relationships with these 
physicians/practitioners. 
Assignment of Benefits and Financial Agreement: 
I certify all information given by me is correct and I accept responsibility 
for the charges for the care provided. I agree to the assignment of all 
third-party benefits to The Medical Center and to any physician, 
practitioner, organization or independent contractor who provided. 
Methods of contact may include the use of pre-recorded or artificial voice 
messages and/or automated dialing. 
Release of Information: 
J authorize the release of all or part of my records, including information 
stored in The Medical Center corporate-wide database, to my physician(s), 
whose name I provided at the time of registration, and to any physician or 
practitioner who has or will provide services to me. I authorize the release 
of statistical information as required by any local, state or federal agency 
or managed care program. I authorize the release of my social security 
number to the manufacturer of any implantable medical device in 
accordance with the Medical Device Tracking Act of the FDA. I authorize 
the release of my HIV and hepatitis test results to health care personnel in 
the event of an occupational exposure. 
I authorize the hospital, physicians and any other holder of medical or 
other information to release any information about me (including medical 
information concerning psychological or psychiatric conditions, 
alcoholism and/or drug related conditions and HIV or other blood-bome 
infectious diseases) required for the completion of any claim for benefits 
arising out of services rendered to me either on an inpatient or outpatient 
basis to any person or corporation which is or may be liable for all or part of 
the total charge incurred, including but not limited to insurance companies, 
the Social Security Administration, its intermediaries and carriers, state 
agencies and workers’ compensation carriers, as well as the review 
organization employed by my employer or the employer of the insured. 
member of my family and any corporation engaged by the hospital to make 
products or services, and agree to pay all charges not covered by collection of any unpaid hospital charges. I further authorize my employer to 
third-party payers. If I am covered by an ERISA plan, with this assignment release to the hospital or any agency engaged for the purpose of collecting 
I specifically authorize my providers to receive copies of all notifications any unpaid hospital charges, verification of my employment status, including 
and information that I am legally entitled to receive under the terms of my the amount of salary or wages and the number of hours worked. 
insurance/health plan and to act on my behalf to appeal benefit

> HC¥ Genotyping l (D) l l \ I 
(D) tla or ib 
Cannot be further subtyped into Type la or Type ib due to 
high conservation of the 5' untranslated region of the HCY 
genome. In addition, Type 6 virus may be misclassified as 
Type 1 in some cases. The Hepatitis C Virus High-Resolution 
Genotype by Sequencing test (ARUP test code 2006898) 
provides a higher level of subtype resolution. 
INTERPRETIVE INFORMATION: Hepatitis C Genotyping 
Hepatitis C Viral RNA is tested using reverse transcription 
polymerase chain reaction (RT-PCR) to amplify a specific 
portion of the 5' untranslated region (5' UTR) of the viral 
genome. The amplified nucleic acid is sequenced 
bi-directionally using dye-terminator chemistry (ABI). 
Sequencing data is compared to a database of characterized 
sequences. 
Isolates of hepatitis C virus are grouped into six major 
genotypes (1-6). These genotypes are subtyped according to 
sequence characteristics. Due to high conservation of the 
5' un-translated region of the HCV genome, this test has 
limitations in differentiating subtype la from 1b. 
Therefore, these subtypes will be reported as la or 1b. In 
rare instances, Type 6 virus may be misclassified as Type 1. 
This test was developed and its performance characteristics 
determined by ARUP Laboratories. It has not been cleared or 
approved by the US Food and Drug Administration. This test 
was performed in a CLIA certified laboratory and is 
intended for clinical purposes. 
Performed By: ARUP Laboratories 
500 Chipeta Way 
Salt Lake City. UT 84108 
Laboratory Director: Tracy I. George, MD

INTERPRETIVE INFORMATION: Fibrometer Interpretation 
Calculations for the final report are based on accurate 
data for age. gender, and platelet count. If any of this 
information needs to be corrected, please contact ARUP 
Client Services to request a recalculation. Client Services 
may be contacted at [PHONE-120]. 
The Echosens FibroMeter profile serves as a surrogate 
marker of liver fibrosis, cirrhosis, and necro-inflammatory 
activity. A proprietary algorithm calculates and compares 
results from 7? blood markers along with age and gender tao 
provide a patient score (from 0 to 1} and a correlated 
fibrosis stage (Metavir FO-F4) and activity grade (Metavir 
A0-A3}. The fibrosis’cirrhosis score is further evaluated 
by a rules-based system to detect anomalous profile results 
which may modify the fibrosis’cirrhosis score as needed. 
Results should be interpreted in conjunction with the 
patient's clinical history: particularly when the 
rules-based system has modified the scores. 
Legend: 
—-Metavir is a histological scoring system for determining 
the extent of liver fibrosis and inflammation. 
STAGE OF FIBROSIS (F scale) 
FO = no fibrosis 
Fl = portal fibrosis without septa 
F2 = portal fibrosis with few septa 
F3 = numerous septa without cirrhosis 
F4 = cirrhosis 
GRADE OF NECRO-INFLAMMATORY ACTIVITY (A scale) 
AO = no activity 
mild activity 
moderate activity 
A3 = severe activity 
—-Platelet count result provided by client.

General Conditions of Admission, Consent, Assignment of Benefits & Financial Agreement 
Consent to Diagnostic Tests, Procedures and Medical Treatment: 
I do voluntarily consent to hospital care involving diagnostic tests, 
procedures and medical treatment as ordered by my treating physician(s), 
practitioner(s) and his or her designees. This consent includes testing for 
communicable diseases, including but not limited to Human 
Immunodeficiency Virus (HIV), hepatitis or any other blood-bome 
infectious disease if ordered for a diagnostic purpose or due to 
occupational exposure of a health care worker. I acknowledge no 
guarantee has been made to me as to the results of examination and 
treatment in the hospital. 
Independent Contractor Acknowledgement: 
I understand and acknowledge the physicians and other practitioners 
involved in my care, including but not limited to my attending 
physician, consulting physicians, emergency department physicians, 
physician assistants, nurse practitioners, radiologists, 
anesthesiologists, nurse anesthetists and pathologists are not agents 
or employees of The Medical Center. I further understand I will be 
billed separately for services by these providers. These providers have 
independent relationships with insurance companies, and the hospital 
makes no guarantee as to any preferred provider relationships with these 
physicians/practitioners. 
Assignment of Benefits and Financial Agreement: 
I certify all information given by me is correct and I accept responsibility 
for the charges for the care provided. I agree to the assignment of all 
third-party benefits to The Medical Center and to any physician, 
practitioner, organization or independent contractor who provided. 
Methods of contact may include the use of pre-recorded or artificial voice 
messages and/or automated dialing. 
Release of Information: 
J authorize the release of all or part of my records, including information 
stored in The Medical Center corporate-wide database, to my physician(s), 
whose name I provided at the time of registration, and to any physician or 
practitioner who has or will provide services to me. I authorize the release 
of statistical information as required by any local, state or federal agency 
or managed care program. I authorize the release of my social security 
number to the manufacturer of any implantable medical device in 
accordance with the Medical Device Tracking Act of the FDA. I authorize 
the release of my HIV and hepatitis test results to health care personnel in 
the event of an occupational exposure. 
I authorize the hospital, physicians and any other holder of medical or 
other information to release any information about me (including medical 
information concerning psychological or psychiatric conditions, 
alcoholism and/or drug related conditions and HIV or other blood-bome 
infectious diseases) required for the completion of any claim for benefits 
arising out of services rendered to me either on an inpatient or outpatient 
basis to any person or corporation which is or may be liable for all or part of 
the total charge incurred, including but not limited to insurance companies, 
the Social Security Administration, its intermediaries and carriers, state 
agencies and workers’ compensation carriers, as well as the review 
organization employed by my employer or the employer of the insured.

PERSONAL PROPERTY ACKNOWLEDGEMENT AND RELEASE 
(No liability for loss of personal property/limitation of liability) 
Hall,Cora Mae 07/13/22 
Patient Date 
The Patient hereby acknowledges and agrees as follows: 
1. The Medical Center provides a safe for the protection of patients' valuables (for example, wallet or 
purse, money, credit cards, driver's license, identification papers, watch, jewelry, etc.). I understand 
that it is my responsibility to inform a Hospital employee if I have any items that I would like to 
deposit in the Hospital's safe and, therefore, agree that the Hospital's maximum total liability for the 
loss of or damage to any of my property placed in the safe is $500.00. I release from liability, 
indemnify and hold the Hospital, its employees, agents and contractors, harmless from any loss, cost 
or damage that I sustain because of any damage to or loss of my personal property that may exceed 
this $500.00 limit. 
2. ILunderstand and agree that the Hospital , its employees, agents and contractors, are not responsible for 
the protection or safekeeping of any items of personal property (for example, personal electronic 
items, eyeglasses, contact lenses, hearing aids, dentures, etc.) which I keep with me in my hospital 
room or in any other area of the Hospital. I acknowledge that it is my responsibility to oversee and 
protect all personal property that remains with me and that I de not provide to the Hospital for deposit 
into the Hospital's safe. I further release from liability, indemnify and hold the Hospital, its 
employees, agents and contractors, harmless from loss, cost or damage that I sustain because of any 
damage to or loss of my personal property that I keep with me during my stay at the Hospital.

INTERPRETIVE INFORMATION: HCV by Quantitative NAAT 
Normal range for this assay is "Not Detected". 
The quantitative range of this assay is 10 - 100,000,000 
IU/mL (1.0 - 8.0 log IU/mL). 
Lower limit of quantitation (L1oQ): 
10 IU/mL (1.0 log IU/mL) 
LLoQ values do not apply to diluted specimens. 
A result of "Not Detected" does not rule out the presence 
of inhibitors in the patient specimen or hepatitis C virus 
RNA concentrations below the level of detection of the 
test. Care should be taken when interpreting any single 
viral load determination. 
This test should not be used for blood donor screening, 
associated re-entry protocols, or for screening Human Cell, 
Tissues and Cellular Tissue-Based Products (HCT/P).

General Conditions of Admission, Consent, Assignment of Benefits & Financial Agreement 
Consent to Diagnostic Tests, Procedures and Medical Treatment: 
I do voluntarily consent to hospital care involving diagnostic tests, 
procedures and medical treatment as ordered by my treating physician(s), 
practitioner(s) and his or her designees. This consent includes testing for 
communicable diseases, including but not limited to Human 
Immunodeficiency Virus (HIV), hepatitis or any other blood-bome 
infectious disease if ordered for a diagnostic purpose or due to 
occupational exposure of a health care worker. I acknowledge no 
guarantee has been made to me as to the results of examination and 
treatment in the hospital. 
Independent Contractor Acknowledgement: 
I understand and acknowledge the physicians and other practitioners 
involved in my care, including but not limited to my attending 
physician, consulting physicians, emergency department physicians, 
physician assistants, nurse practitioners, radiologists, 
anesthesiologists, nurse anesthetists and pathologists are not agents 
or employees of The Medical Center. I further understand I will be 
billed separately for services by these providers. These providers have 
independent relationships with insurance companies, and the hospital 
makes no guarantee as to any preferred provider relationships with these 
physicians/practitioners. 
Assignment of Benefits and Financial Agreement: 
I certify all information given by me is correct and I accept responsibility 
for the charges for the care provided. I agree to the assignment of all 
third-party benefits to The Medical Center and to any physician, 
practitioner, organization or independent contractor who provided. 
Methods of contact may include the use of pre-recorded or artificial voice 
messages and/or automated dialing. 
Release of Information:

stored in The Medical Center corporate-wide database, to my physician(s), 
whose name I provided at the time of registration, and to any physician or 
practitioner who has or will provide services to me. I authorize the release 
of statistical information as required by any local, state or federal agency 
or managed care program. I authorize the release of my social security 
number to the manufacturer of any implantable medical device in 
accordance with the Medical Device Tracking Act of the FDA. I authorize 
the release of my HIV and hepatitis test results to health care personnel in 
the event of an occupational exposure. 
I authorize the hospital, physicians and any other holder of medical or 
other information to release any information about me (including medical 
information concerning psychological or psychiatric conditions, 
alcoholism and/or drug related conditions and HIV or other blood-bome

PERSONAL PROPERTY ACKNOWLEDGEMENT AND RELEASE 
(No liability for loss of personal property/limitation of liability) 
Hall,Cora Mae 12/08/22 
Patient Date 
The Patient hereby acknowledges and agrees as follows: 
1. The Medical Center provides a safe for the protection of patients' valuables (for example, wallet or 
purse, money, credit cards, driver's license, identification papers, watch, jewelry, etc.). I understand 
that it is my responsibility to inform a Hospital employee if I have any items that I would like to 
deposit in the Hospital's safe and, therefore, agree that the Hospital's maximum total liability for the 
loss of or damage to any of my property placed in the safe is $500.00. I release from liability, 
indemnify and hold the Hospital, its employees, agents and contractors, harmless from any loss, cost 
or damage that I sustain because of any damage to or loss of my personal property that may exceed 
this $500.00 limit. 
2. ILunderstand and agree that the Hospital , its employees, agents and contractors, are not responsible for 
the protection or safekeeping of any items of personal property (for example, personal electronic 
items, eyeglasses, contact lenses, hearing aids, dentures, etc.) which I keep with me in my hospital 
room or in any other area of the Hospital. I acknowledge that it is my responsibility to oversee and

angulated displaced left distal radius fracture. I discussed options with surgical and nonsurgical. She! 
would like to proceed with an ORIF procedure of the left distal radius, She is right-hand dominant. : '

regarding further options non-surgical and surgical today. Informed consent was discussed at length 
and the patient verbalized a thorough understanding of all options and the surgical procedure. All 
surgical and nonsurgical options with risks, benefits, potential complications and outcomes were ' 
discussed at length with the patient. They had all their questions answered to satisfactlon. They do 
understand risks of the procedure which include stiffness, pain, infection, neurovascular Injury, re- ' ; 
tear and possible hardware failure. Preoperative clearance will be done prior to surgery. All 
preoperative paperwork was done including consents'which were signed by the patient, They do. 
agree to proceed with the procedure. Fu rthermore, the patient does understand the peri- operative 
and post-operative course, They do understand the rehabilitation and potential therapy that is , 
involved in achieving an optimal outcome. They also understand the tlme period involved in full

Promethazine tablets 
What is this medicine? 
PROMETHAZINE (proe METH a zeen) is an antihistamine. It is used to treat allergic reactions and 
to treat or prevent nausea and vomiting from illness or motion sickness. It is also used to make 
you sleep before surgery, and to help treat pain or nausea after surgery. 
How should I use this medicine? 
Take this medicine by mouth with a glass of water. Follow the directions on the prescription label. 
Take your doses at regular intervals. Do not take your medicine more often than directed. 
Talk to your pediatrician regarding the use of this medicine in children. Special care may be 
needed. This medicine should not be given to infants and children younger than 2 years old. 
What side effects may I notice from receiving this medicine? 
Side effects that you should report to your doctor or health care professional as soon as possible: 
® blurred vision 
@ jrregular heartbeat, palpitations or chest pain 
muscle or facial twitches 
pain or difficulty passing urine 
seizures 
skin rash 
slowed or shallow breathing 
unusual bleeding or bruising 
yellowing of the eyes or skin 
Side effects that usually do not require medical attention (report to your doctor or health care 
professional if they continue or are bothersome): 
@ headache 
® nightmares, agitation, nervousness, excitability, not able to sleep (these are more likely in 
children) 
® stuffy nose 
What may interact with this medicine? 
Do not take this medicine with any of the following medications: 
® cisapride 
® dofetilide 
® dronedarone 
® MAOIs like Carbex, Eldepryl, Marplan, Nardil, Parnate 
® pimozide 
® quinidine, including dextromethorphan; quinidine 

Page 2 of 3 
Name: Cora Mae Hall 
Acct Num: L00039407077 
ts wep 7 ed Rec Num: The Medical Center Lean: Bc ambulatory Surge 
HEALTH 
Primary Provider: Malempati,Chaitanya 
Ss 
Date: 12/08/22 
® thioridazine 
® ziprasidone 
This medicine may also interact with the following medications: 
certain medicines for depression, anxiety, or psychotic disturbances 
certain medicines for anxiety or sleep 
certain medicines for seizures like carbamazepine, phenobarbital, phenytoin 
certain medicines for movement abnormalities as in Parkinson's disease, or for 
gastrointestinal problems 
epinephrine 
medicines for allergies or colds 
muscle relaxants 
narcotic medicines for pain 
other medicines that prolong the QT interval (cause an abnormal heart rhythm) 
® tramadol 
® trimethobenzamide 
What if I miss a dose? 
If you miss a dose, take it as soon as you can. If it is almost time for your next dose, take only 
that dose. Do not take double or extra doses. 
Where should I keep my medicine? 
Keep out of the reach of children. 
Store at room temperature, between 20 and 25 degrees C (68 and 77 degrees F). Protect from 
light. Throw away any unused medicine after the expiration date. 
What should I tell my health care provider before I take this medicine? 
They need to know if you have any of these conditions: 
® glaucoma 
® high blood pressure or heart disease 
®@ kidney disease 
® liver disease 
® lung or breathing disease, like asthma 
® prostate trouble 
® pain or difficulty passing urine 
® seizures 
® an unusual or allergic reaction to promethazine or phenothiazines, other medicines, foods, 
dyes, or preservatives 
® pregnant or trying to get pregnant 
® breast-feeding 
What should I watch for while using this medicine?

Tell your doctor or health care professional if your symptoms do not start to get better in 1 to 2 
days. 
You may get drowsy or dizzy. Do not drive, use machinery, or do anything that needs mental 
alertness until you know how this medicine affects you. To reduce the risk of dizzy or fainting 
spells, do not stand or sit up quickly, especially if you are an older patient. Alcohol may increase 
dizziness and drowsiness. Avoid alcoholic drinks. 
Your mouth may get dry. Chewing sugarless gum or sucking hard candy, and drinking plenty of 
water may help. Contact your doctor if the problem does not go away or is severe. 
This medicine may cause dry eyes and blurred vision. If you wear contact lenses you may feel 
some discomfort. Lubricating drops may help. See your eye doctor if the problem does not go 
away or is severe. 
This medicine can make you more sensitive to the sun. Keep out of the sun. If you cannot avoid 
being in the sun, wear protective clothing and use sunscreen. Do not use sun lamps or tanning 
beds/booths. 
If you are diabetic, check your blood-sugar levels regularly.

Norco Oral Tablet 10 mg/325 mg 
Uses 
For pain. 
Instructions 
This medicine may be taken with or without food. 
Keep the medicine at room temperature. Avoid heat and direct light. 
To reduce constipation, eat high fiber foods, drink plenty of water and exercise. 
Please tell your doctor and pharmacist about all the medicines you take. Include both prescription 
and over-the-counter medicines. Also tell them about any vitamins, herbal medicines, or anything 
else you take for your health. 
It is very important that you follow your doctor's instructions for all blood tests. 
Do not take more than 6 pills in a day. 
Cautions 
This medicine contains an opioid. Though it helps many people, this medicine may sometimes 
cause addiction, especially if it is used for a long time. This risk for addiction may be higher if you 
have a substance use disorder - such as overuse of or addiction to drugs or alcohol. Speak with 
your doctor about the benefits and risks of using this medicine. 
Ask your doctor or pharmacist if you should have naloxone on hand to treat opioid overdose. 
Teach your family or household members about the signs of an opioid overdose and how to treat 
it. 
If you stop this medicine suddenly, after using it regularly for a long time, you may have 
withdrawal symptoms. Your doctor may ask you to slowly reduce your dose before stopping it. 
Tell your doctor right away if you notice any symptoms of withdrawal. Withdrawal symptoms can 
include unusual sweating, watering eyes, runny nose, chills, stomach pain, diarrhea, yawning, 
muscle aches, irritability, restlessness, anxiety, trouble sleeping, or thoughts of suicide. 
Tell your doctor and pharmacist if you ever had an allergic reaction to a medicine. Symptoms of 
an allergic reaction can include trouble breathing, skin rash, itching, swelling, or severe dizziness. 
Do not use the medication any more than instructed. 
If possible, avoid using with marijuana or other medicines that can cause dizziness or drowsiness. 
These include allergy/cold products, muscle relaxers, sleep aids, and pain relievers. 
Your ability to stay alert or to react quickly may be impaired by this medicine. Do not operate

Tell the doctor or pharmacist if you are pregnant, planning to be pregnant, or breastfeeding. 
This medicine can hurt a new baby in the womb. If you become pregnant while on this medicine, 
tell your doctor immediately. Your doctor may switch you to a different medicine. 
Ask your pharmacist if this medicine can interact with any of your other medicines. Be sure to tell 
them about all the medicines you take. 
Please tell all your doctors and dentists that you are on this medicine before they provide care. 
Do not start or stop any other medicines without first speaking to your doctor or pharmacist. 
This medicine should be used with caution in patients with breathing difficulties. 
Call your doctor right away if you notice slow or shallow breathing. 
Do not share this medicine with anyone who has not been prescribed this medicine. 
This medicine contains acetaminophen. There are many medicines with acetaminophen. Taking 
these medicines together can cause you to get too much acetaminophen. This can cause serious 
liver problems. Look carefully on the package of all your medicines to see if acetaminophen is 
included. Ask your pharmacist which medicines you can take safely. 
Side Effects

doctor about what you should do if you experience these or other side effects.

stomach upset or abdominal pain 
sweating

If you have any of the following side effects, you may be getting too much medicine. Please 
contact your doctor to let them know about these side effects. 
® changes in memory, mood, or thinking 
® difficulty concentrating

seek medical help quickly.

GENERAL ANESTHESIA/SEDATION D/C INSTRUCT 
You may experience lightheadedness, dizziness and sleepiness following or sedation. 
- Do not drive or operate heavy machinery for 24 hours. 
- Do not consume alcohol, tranquilizers, sleeping medications, or any non-prescribed medication 
for 24 hours. 
- Do not make important decisions or sign any important documents in the next 24 hours. 
- Aresponsible adult should remain with you for the rest of today or tonight. 
- Children may appear flushed for several hours after surgery/sedation. 
SURGICAL PATIENT 
- Avoid stress to the suture line such as pulling, pushing, etc. 
- You are advised to go home from the hospital. Restrict your activities and rest for a day. 
Resume light to normal activity tomorrow as directed. 
Do not engage in strenuous activity that may place stress on your incision. 
DIET 
Unless instructed otherwise begin with clear liquids, bouillon, dry toast or soda crackers. If not 
nauseated you may begin a regular diet when you desire. Greasy and spicy foods are not 
advised. 
SPECIFIC COMPLICATIONS TO WATCH AND NOTIFY M.D. FOR: 
-Fever over 101 degrees Fahrenheit. 
-Pain not relieved by medication ordered. 
-Swelling around operative site. 
-Increased redness, warmth, hardness, around operative site. 
-Such signs and symptoms may become apparent only after 36-48 hours. 
-Slight discomfort at the IV sight is normal, Application of a warm, moist cloth will be helpful. 
-Numb, tingling or cold fingers or toes. 
-Blood-soaked dressing. (Small amounts of oozing may be normal.) 
-Increasing and progressive drainage from surgical area or exam site. 
-Inability to urinate.

Bladder Care after Outpatient Surgery 
Caring for your Bladder after Outpatient Surgery 
Sometimes surgery and anesthesia medicines can affect your bladder for several hours. This 
information will help you care for your bladder after you are discharged home. The inability to 
empty your bladder after surgery, a condition called urinary retention, is considered an 
emergency if you are no longer in the hospital. If you are unable to empty your bladder within 
6-8 hours from the time your surgery ended, you should seek treatment from your local 
emergency room. This time is am/pm. 
How does surgery affect my bladder? 
- Surgery can cause a temporary interruption of nerve impulses from the brain to the bladder, 
decreasing the sensation and feeling that you need to urinate. 
- Temporary swelling after surgery can also affect your ability to empty your bladder. 
- When the bladder gets full and can hold no more urine, it can cause stretching of the bladder 
which can cause damage to the bladder muscles. When the bladder can hold no more urine, fluid 
backs up into the kidneys, which can also cause damage. 
What can I do if I can’t urinate? 
- Try running the water in the sink. Sometimes the sound of running water helps. 
- Sit in a warm bath or get into the shower (if not contraindicated by your procedure). 
- Try placing your hands in cold water. 
- Walk. Walk. Walk. 
- Do not keep drinking large amounts of fluid if you feel like your bladder is full and you cannot 
empty it. 
- GO TO YOUR LOCAL EMERGENCY ROOM

DATE OF PROCEDURE: [DOB-158] 
PREOPERATIVE DIAGNOSIS: Closed displaced comminuted intraarticular left distal 
radius fracture. 
POSTOPERATIVE DIAGNOSIS: Closed displaced comminuted intraarticular left distal 
radius fracture. 
PROCEDURE: Open reduction and internal fixation of left distal radius using a 
Stryker distal radius locking plate. 
SURGEON: Chaitanya Malempati, D.O. 
FIRST ASSISTANT: Nicasio Villarreal Jr, KCSA 
ANESTHESIA: General. 
COMPLICATIONS: None. 
ESTIMATED BLOOD LOSS: Less than 5 mL. 
TOURNIQUET TIME: 40 minutes. 
INDICATION: The patient is a pleasant 33-year-old female who sustained a fall and 
had left distal radius fracture. Failed non-operative modalities. 1 reviewed 
imaging with the patient. She elected to proceed with ORIF procedure. All 
surgical and non-surgical options with risks, benefits, potential complications, 
and outcomes were discussed in length with the patient. She understcod and all 
questions were answered. She did sign consents for the procedure and blood 
products and agreed to proceed with the procedure. 
DESCRIPTION OF PROCEDURE: The procedure was discussed between the operative 
surgeon and the patient in the preoperative area. They both agreed to proceed with 
the procedure and signed consents for the procedure and blood products. The left 
upper extremity was marked. The patient was brought back to the operative suite, 
transferred from the gurney to the operating room table and positioned 
appropriately for the procedure. A surgical time-out was performed with the 
operative surgeon in the room. General anesthesia was administered per 
Anesthesiology. The left upper extremity was prepped and draped in the appropriate 
sterile fashion. An Esmarch was used to exsanguinate the limb and tourniquet was 
inflated to 250 mmHg. 
! made a volar FCR approach with a #15 blade scalpel through the skin, subcutaneous

tissue, and subcutaneous fat and continued dissection was performed very carefully. 
! retracted the FCR tendon appropriately. 1 then accessed the fracture site, 
cleaned out using a curette and copiously irrigated using normal saline. ! 
performed a reduction maneuver with a Freer. Once found to be reduced in the AP, 
lateral, and fluoroscopic views, ! placed a Stryker distal radius locking plate. 
Three proximal cortical screws and seven distal locking screws were placed. Final 
images were taken showing good reduction of the fracture and good positioning of 
plate and screws. Copious irrigation was performed. 0 Vicryl suture for deep 
tissue, 2-0 Vicryl for subcutaneous tissue and 3-0 nylon suture on the skin. 
Cleaned and dried appropriately. Dressed using Xeroform, 4x4's, ABDs, Sof-Rol, and 
a well-padded volar plaster splint. Drapes were removed. Tourniquet was deflated. 
The patient was transferred from the operating table to the gurney and to the PACU 
for recovery. There were no complications from anesthesia at any portion of the 
procedure. 
DISPOSITION: She will be discharged home from the PACU once stable. All discharge 
instructions will be given ta the patient at discharge including pain medication 
and nausea medication scripts. The patient will be non-weightbearing on left upper 
extremity. Follow up in postoperative clinic in two weeks. Keep the splint on and 
clean, dry and intact. Antibiotics for infection prophylaxis.

Physician Instructions: ***,. Instruct patients who are presently on thyroid, seizure, steroid, heart, blood 
pressure (except ACE inhibitors), or breathing medication to take these medications 
as routine on the morning of surgery With 15 ml or less of water immediately upon awakenmg; they are not to take any medications other than these until after 
surgery. *** *** Instruct patients who routinely use inhalers to bring them to the hospital If currently on home nebulizer inhalation therapy, instruct ta do treatment before coming to the hospital. five days prior to surgery. ***

LO00617236 
Protocol text: For patients with a history of diabetes or blood glucose greater than 180 mg/dL: 
1. Accu-chek every 2 hours while in pre-op and post-op recovery areas 2. If insulin is given, check blood glucose prior to discharge 3. Prior to surgery, notify the anesthesiologist of the DOSE and TIME insulin is given. 4. Use Insulin-Sensitive Protocol for patients with any of the following: 
- Age over 70 years - Chronic renal insufficiency or creatinine greater than 1.5 mg/dL - History of more than one episode of hypoglycemia in 3 months 
5. Follow hypoglycemia pratocol for blaod sugar less than 70 
* Call MD if used * If alert, juice or a light snack (only if patient is post-operative) * Repeat Accu-chek and retreat with juice or light snack every 15 minutes 
until blood sugar is greater than 70 mg/dL 
* If unable to take PO and IV in place: 1 syringe D50 (25 GM 
* Repeat Accu-chek and retreat with 1 syringe of D50 every 15 minutes 
until blood sugar is greater than 70 mg/dL 
* If unable to take PO and no IV in place: Glucagon lmg IM and start IV 
* If no response by the time IV is started, give 1 syringe of DSO (25 GM) 
every 15 minutes until blood sugar is greater than 70 mg/dL 
Dose Intruction: Perioperative Humalog Sliding Scale while in pre-op and post-op recovery areas: 
BS 0-180 = NO INSULIN BS 181-220 = 3 UNITS (2 UNITS IF INSULIN-SENSITIVE) BS 221-260 = 4 UNITS (3 UNITS IF INSULIN-SENSITIVE) BS 261-300 = 6 UNITS (4 UNITS IF INSULIN-SENSITIVE) BS 301-350 = 8 UNITS (5 UNITS IF INSULIN-SENSITIVE) BS 351-400 = 10 UNITS (6 UNITS IF INSULIN-SENSITIVE) BS >400 = 12 UNITS (8 UNITS IF INSULIN-SENSITIVE)

FOR PATIENTS WITH DIAGNOSED OSA REQUIRING HOME PAP/SUPPLEMENTAL OXYGEN OR HIGH RISK OSA PATIENTS (SBAT>3) 
if patient shows -Initiate and titrate PAP therapy (home setting or 8-12 cm H20) 
signs of the following (DO NOT USE FOR UPPER AIRWAY, NASAL, OR BARIATRIC PROCEDURES) : 
*Obstruction, episodes of apnea, and loud snoring 
*Low oxygen saturations (<92%) that cannot be resolved with oxygen and use of oral or 
nasal airway 
*Difficulty arousing patient, maintaining eye or verbal contact -Place patient in non-supine position throughout recovery process if feasible. -If oxygen saturation persistently <88% on oxygen support and/or change in level of 
consciousness (LOC) please call RT to obtain ABG and contact anesthesia. 
-Patients having airway surgery (i.e UPPP), upper abdominal surgery, or tonsillectomy (age <3) must be admitted post-operatively. 
-If patient requiring PAP support or supplemental oxygen after one hour of PACU time, 
please contact anesthesia for in-person assessment/sign-out. 
-If patient requires CPAP at any point during PACU stay, please place continuous 
oxygen therapy and standard monitoring including pulse oximetry in Phase 2 recavery 
area until patient is ambulatory or can maintain room air Sa02 >90%. 
-If at risk patient has episode of oxygen desaturation that occurs during phase 2 
(<90%), 
anesthesia. 
recovery additional hour must be added to recovery time. Please notify 
-Patient must be able to maintain baseline O2 saturations on room air for >30 min 
prior to Phase 2 discharge. 
-Outpatient surgery patients are required to have adult supervision at home for 24 
hours post-operatively.

*Live* Commonwealth Health Cor Patient Order Summary Page: 33 of 43

L00039407077 Hall,Cora Mae Location: BGM Ambulatory Surgery Medical Record Number: LO00617236 
33/E Attending: Malempati,Chaitanya 5, DO Account Number: LOOO39407077 
Reason: ORIF of Left Distal Radius Registration: 12/08/22 
Category Order Status Start Ord Provider Entered By 
Protocol text: For patients with a history of diabetes or blood glucose greater than 180 mg/dL: 
1. Accu-chek every 2 hours while in pre-op and post-op recovery areas 2. If insulin is given, check blood glucose prior to discharge 3. Prior to surgery, notify the anesthesiologist of the DOSE and TIME insulin is given. 4. Use Insulin-Sensitive Protocol for patients with any of the following: 
- Age over 70 years - Chronic renal insufficiency or creatinine greater than 1.5 mg/dL - History of more than one episode of hypoglycemia in 3 months 
5. Follow hypoglycemia pratocol for blaod sugar less than 70 
* Call MD if used * If alert, juice or a light snack (only if patient is post-operative) * Repeat Accu-chek and retreat with juice or light snack every 15 minutes 
until blood sugar is greater than 70 mg/dL 
* If unable to take PO and IV in place: 1 syringe D50 (25 GM 
* Repeat Accu-chek and retreat with 1 syringe of D50 every 15 minutes 
until blood sugar is greater than 70 mg/dL 
* If unable to take PO and no IV in place: Glucagon lmg IM and start IV 
* If no response by the time IV is started, give 1 syringe of DSO (25 GM) 
every 15 minutes until blood sugar is greater than 70 mg/dL 
Dose Intruction: 1 syringe = 25 gm Label Comments: Perioperative Insulin Sliding Scale; for treatment of hypoglycemia per protocol while in 
pre-ap and post-op recovery areas

procedure or treatment or recuperation period, and the risks which may be involved; (3) the likelihood 
of achieving treatment goals; and (4) the possible alternative methods of treatment, along with the 
benefits, risks and side effects associated with the alternatives, including not having the procedure or 
treatment performed. 
H 
I authorize and direct my doctor(s) and associates or assistants, any healthcare provider or healthcare 
provider in training and The Medical Center to provide such additional services as they deem necessary, 
including, but not limited to, the administration or maintenance of anesthesia (including sedation ' 
anal gesia), and the performance of services involving pathology and radiology. I understand medical _! 
services may be performed by physicians or other persons who are not agents or employees of The 
Medical Center, but are independent contractors, and I may be billed separately for their services. 
I understand there are inherent risks with the administration of anesthesia. The doctor, anesthesiologist, 
nurse anesthetist or nurse practitioner has explained the risks, benefits and alternative methods of 
anesthesia. Complications associated with all types of anesthesia include, but are not limited to, damage 
to teeth, lips, nose, throat, voice box, windpipe, eyes, nerves or blood vessels. Drug reactions can occur 
and may be minor or serious. Very serious complications, including paralysis, brain damage or death are 
uncommon, but can occur. 
For the purposes of advancing medical education, I consent to the admittance of observers to the 
operating room or room where the procedure is being performed and to the photography or televising of 
the procedure to be performed, if my identity is not revealed. I understand a sales representative from a 
company that furnishes medical equipment may be present in the operating room forthe purpose of = 
observing, advising and/or demonstrating a device. :

Any tissue, organ, extremity or other body part surgically removed may be disposed of by The Medical 
Center in accordance with its usual practice. 
Some procedures may require a transfusion of blood or blood products. I understand a blood transfusion 
is when blood or blood products are given through a sterile needle into one of my veins. I have been 
informed of the benefits, alternatives and risks involved in receiving a blood transfusion. The possible 
risks include, but are not limited to, reactions such as: bruising, swelling, infection or bleeding at the 
needle site; headache, fever, itching or a rash; volume overload which could affect the heart or lungs; 
_ and rarely, transmission of diseases such as HIV, AIDS and hepatitis, which require lengthy treatment 
and can be fatal. (Although the procedures for screening blood products for diseases such as HIV, AIDS 
and: hepatitis are effective, no process or testing is 100% reliable.)

Th Medical PREOPERATIVE PREGNANCY TESTING 
Center Education, Consent and/or Refusal of Testing 
BOWLING GREEH - SCOTTSVILLE » FRANKLIN 
This is to educate female patients within childbearing years undergoing surgery of the potential dangers of anesthesia on a 
fetus. Exposure to anesthestic agents within the first trimester (first 3 months) of pregnancy may have possible adverse \ 
effects on the fetus. 
H 
Studies from the American Society of Anesthesiologists, the Centers for Disease Control and others differ on their } 
analysis & findings. However, studies have shown there may be a possibility of an increase in hydrocephalus (an increase 
in cerebrospinal fluid in the ventricles of the brain), a possible increase chance of neuro tubal defect (a defect effecting the 
spinal cord and brain) and other effects (malformations) that can occur when the fetus has been exposed to certain 
anesthestic agents in the first trimester. Also, there could be spontaneous abortion or possible stillbirth. 
Ambulatory Surgery and The Anesthesia Department are providing this information to you so you understand the re: 
for pregnancy screening prior to surgery. Initial 
CRYFERIA FOR TESTING: (Yes to any, requires pregnancy testing, check on Anesthesia orders) 
ae there any possibility you could be pregnant? 
Are you experiencing a monthly cycle? H : 
Q Are you experiencing irregular or missed cycles? 
Q Tubal Ligation 
CRITERIA FOR NOT TESTING: (Yes to any, requires no pregnancy testing) 
QO >S50 years old / no cycle for 12 months 
QO Hysterectomy 
Q Documented by MD there is no need 
I have read this and understand the potential effects anesthesia can have on a fetus. I have answered truthfully the 
questions "C and I hereby,consent to the pregnancy testing i

For patients with a history of diabetes or blood glucose 
greater than 180 mg/dL: 
1. Accu-chek every 2 hours while in pre-op and post-op 
recovery areas 
2. If insulin is given, check blood glucose prior to 
discharge 
3. Prior to surgery. notify the anesthesiologist of the 
DOSE and TIME insulin is given. 
4. Use Insulin-Sensitive Protocol for patients with any af 
the following: 
— Age over 70 years 
— Chronic renal insufficiency or creatinine greater 
than 1.5 mg“dL 
— History of more than one episode of hypoglycemia in 
3 months 
&. Follow hypoglycemia protocol for blood sugar less than 
70

sugar 18 greater than 70 ng/dL
